import math

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import triton
import triton.language as tl


@triton.jit
def _paged_attn_decode_split_kernel(
    out_partial_ptr,
    m_partial_ptr,
    l_partial_ptr,
    q_ptr,
    kv_cache_ptr,
    block_table_ptr,
    seq_lens_ptr,
    scale,
    stride_qb,
    stride_qh,
    stride_qd,
    stride_kvn,
    stride_kvp,
    stride_kvh,
    stride_bt_b,
    stride_bt_p,
    stride_op_b,
    stride_op_kv,
    stride_op_c,
    stride_mp_b,
    stride_mp_kv,
    stride_mp_c,
    NUM_HEADS: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_KV_HEADS: tl.constexpr,
    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
    GROUP_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,
    CHUNK_PAGES: tl.constexpr,
    PAGES_PER_TILE: tl.constexpr,
):
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_kv = tl.program_id(1)
    pid_chunk = tl.program_id(2)

    seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b)
    num_pages = (seq_len + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE
    chunk_start_page = pid_chunk * CHUNK_PAGES

    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM
    offs_g = tl.arange(0, GROUP_SIZE)
    q_h = pid_kv * GROUP_SIZE + offs_g

    q_ptrs = q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + q_h[:, None] * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :]
    q = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=mask_d[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)

    base_out = pid_b * stride_op_b + pid_kv * stride_op_kv + pid_chunk * stride_op_c
    base_mp = pid_b * stride_mp_b + pid_kv * stride_mp_kv + pid_chunk * stride_mp_c

    if chunk_start_page >= num_pages:
        tl.store(out_partial_ptr + base_out + offs_g[:, None] * BLOCK_D + offs_d[None, :],
                 tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D), tl.float32), mask=mask_d[None, :])
        tl.store(m_partial_ptr + base_mp + offs_g[:, None],
                 tl.full((GROUP_SIZE, 1), float("-inf"), tl.float32))
        tl.store(l_partial_ptr + base_mp + offs_g[:, None],
                 tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE, 1), tl.float32))
        return

    chunk_end_page = tl.minimum((pid_chunk + 1) * CHUNK_PAGES, num_pages)

    m = tl.full((GROUP_SIZE, 1), float("-inf"), tl.float32)
    l = tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE, 1), tl.float32)
    acc = tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D), tl.float32)

    offs_n = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
    offs_n_big = tl.arange(0, PAGES_PER_TILE * PAGE_SIZE)

    for p in range(chunk_start_page, chunk_end_page, PAGES_PER_TILE):
        page_idx0 = tl.load(block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + p * stride_bt_p)
        kv_base0 = kv_cache_ptr + page_idx0 * stride_kvn + pid_kv * stride_kvh
        remain0 = seq_len - p * PAGE_SIZE
        mask_n0 = offs_n < remain0

        k_ptrs0 = kv_base0 + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :]
        k0 = tl.load(k_ptrs0, mask=mask_n0[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)
        v_ptrs0 = kv_base0 + HEAD_DIM + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :]
        v0 = tl.load(v_ptrs0, mask=mask_n0[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)

        p1 = p + 1
        valid1 = p1 < chunk_end_page
        page_idx1 = tl.load(block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + p1 * stride_bt_p, mask=valid1, other=0)
        kv_base1 = kv_cache_ptr + page_idx1 * stride_kvn + pid_kv * stride_kvh
        remain1 = seq_len - p1 * PAGE_SIZE
        mask_n1 = offs_n < remain1

        k_ptrs1 = kv_base1 + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :]
        k1 = tl.load(k_ptrs1, mask=mask_n1[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)
        v_ptrs1 = kv_base1 + HEAD_DIM + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :]
        v1 = tl.load(v_ptrs1, mask=mask_n1[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)

        k = tl.cat(k0, k1, axis=0)
        v = tl.cat(v0, v1, axis=0)
        mask_n_big = tl.cat(mask_n0, mask_n1, axis=0)

        scores = scale * tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k)).to(tl.float32)
        scores = tl.where(mask_n_big[None, :], scores, float("-inf"))

        m_new = tl.maximum(m, tl.max(scores, axis=1)[:, None])
        alpha = tl.exp(m - m_new)
        p_acc = tl.exp(scores - m_new)
        l = l * alpha + tl.sum(p_acc, axis=1)[:, None]
        acc = acc * alpha + tl.dot(p_acc.to(tl.bfloat16), v).to(tl.float32)
        m = m_new

    tl.store(out_partial_ptr + base_out + offs_g[:, None] * BLOCK_D + offs_d[None, :],
             acc, mask=mask_d[None, :])
    tl.store(m_partial_ptr + base_mp + offs_g[:, None], m)
    tl.store(l_partial_ptr + base_mp + offs_g[:, None], l)


@triton.jit
def _paged_attn_decode_reduce_kernel(
    out_ptr,
    out_partial_ptr,
    m_partial_ptr,
    l_partial_ptr,
    stride_ob,
    stride_oh,
    stride_od,
    stride_op_b,
    stride_op_kv,
    stride_op_c,
    stride_mp_b,
    stride_mp_kv,
    stride_mp_c,
    NUM_HEADS: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_KV_HEADS: tl.constexpr,
    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
    GROUP_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,
    NUM_CHUNKS: tl.constexpr,
):
    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
    pid_kv = tl.program_id(1)

    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM
    offs_g = tl.arange(0, GROUP_SIZE)
    q_h = pid_kv * GROUP_SIZE + offs_g

    m_global = tl.full((GROUP_SIZE, 1), float("-inf"), tl.float32)
    l_global = tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE, 1), tl.float32)
    acc_global = tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D), tl.float32)

    for c in range(NUM_CHUNKS):
        base_out = pid_b * stride_op_b + pid_kv * stride_op_kv + c * stride_op_c
        base_mp = pid_b * stride_mp_b + pid_kv * stride_mp_kv + c * stride_mp_c

        m_c = tl.load(m_partial_ptr + base_mp + offs_g[:, None])
        l_c = tl.load(l_partial_ptr + base_mp + offs_g[:, None])
        acc_c = tl.load(
            out_partial_ptr + base_out + offs_g[:, None] * BLOCK_D + offs_d[None, :],
            mask=mask_d[None, :], other=0.0
        ).to(tl.float32)

        m_new = tl.maximum(m_global, m_c)
        alpha_g = tl.exp(m_global - m_new)
        alpha_c = tl.exp(m_c - m_new)
        acc_global = acc_global * alpha_g + acc_c * alpha_c
        l_global = l_global * alpha_g + l_c * alpha_c
        m_global = m_new

    out = (acc_global / l_global).to(tl.bfloat16)
    out_ptrs = out_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + q_h[:, None] * stride_oh + offs_d[None, :]
    tl.store(out_ptrs, out, mask=mask_d[None, :])


class Model(nn.Module):
    def __init__(
        self,
        batch: int,
        num_heads: int,
        num_kv_heads: int,
        head_dim: int,
        seq_len: int,
        page_size: int,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0
        self.batch = batch
        self.num_heads = num_heads
        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
        self.head_dim = head_dim
        self.seq_len = seq_len
        self.page_size = page_size
        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False)

    def forward(
        self,
        query: torch.Tensor,
        kv_cache: torch.Tensor,
        block_table: torch.Tensor,
        seq_lens: torch.Tensor,
    ) -> torch.Tensor:
        B, H, D = query.shape
        Hkv = self.num_kv_heads
        P = self.page_size
        G = self.group_size

        out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=query.dtype, device=query.device)

        block_d = max(64, 1 << (D - 1).bit_length()) if D > 0 else 64

        # Larger tiles help small head_dim cases utilise tensor cores better.
        if D <= 64:
            pages_per_tile = 2
        else:
            pages_per_tile = 1

        chunk_pages = 16
        chunk_tokens = chunk_pages * P
        max_seq_len = int(seq_lens.max().item())
        num_chunks = (max_seq_len + chunk_tokens - 1) // chunk_tokens
        if num_chunks < 1:
            num_chunks = 1

        partial_shape = (B, Hkv, num_chunks, G, block_d)
        stat_shape = (B, Hkv, num_chunks, G)
        out_partial = torch.empty(partial_shape, dtype=torch.float32, device=query.device)
        m_partial = torch.empty(stat_shape, dtype=torch.float32, device=query.device)
        l_partial = torch.empty(stat_shape, dtype=torch.float32, device=query.device)

        stride_op_b = Hkv * num_chunks * G * block_d
        stride_op_kv = num_chunks * G * block_d
        stride_op_c = G * block_d
        stride_mp_b = Hkv * num_chunks * G
        stride_mp_kv = num_chunks * G
        stride_mp_c = G

        grid_split = (B, Hkv, num_chunks)
        _paged_attn_decode_split_kernel[grid_split](
            out_partial,
            m_partial,
            l_partial,
            query,
            kv_cache,
            block_table,
            seq_lens,
            self.scale,
            query.stride(0),
            query.stride(1),
            query.stride(2),
            kv_cache.stride(0),
            kv_cache.stride(1),
            kv_cache.stride(2),
            block_table.stride(0),
            block_table.stride(1),
            stride_op_b,
            stride_op_kv,
            stride_op_c,
            stride_mp_b,
            stride_mp_kv,
            stride_mp_c,
            NUM_HEADS=H,
            NUM_KV_HEADS=Hkv,
            HEAD_DIM=D,
            PAGE_SIZE=P,
            GROUP_SIZE=G,
            BLOCK_D=block_d,
            CHUNK_PAGES=chunk_pages,
            PAGES_PER_TILE=pages_per_tile,
        )

        grid_reduce = (B, Hkv)
        _paged_attn_decode_reduce_kernel[grid_reduce](
            out,
            out_partial,
            m_partial,
            l_partial,
            out.stride(0),
            out.stride(1),
            out.stride(2),
            stride_op_b,
            stride_op_kv,
            stride_op_c,
            stride_mp_b,
            stride_mp_kv,
            stride_mp_c,
            NUM_HEADS=H,
            NUM_KV_HEADS=Hkv,
            HEAD_DIM=D,
            PAGE_SIZE=P,
            GROUP_SIZE=G,
            BLOCK_D=block_d,
            NUM_CHUNKS=num_chunks,
        )

        return out

stdout (3065 chars) — TRUNCATED
1	"""SOTA reference for paged-attention decode.
2	
3	Tries, in order:
4	  1. FlashInfer's BatchDecodeWithPagedKVCacheWrapper (preferred -- portable,
5	     supports SM120, GQA, arbitrary head_dim).
6	  2. vLLM's paged_attention_v2 CUDA op (requires its KV-cache layout, more
7	     finicky; we adapt the layout on the fly when possible).
8

1	"""Naive PyTorch paged-attention decode reference (correctness oracle, not SOTA).
2	
3	Single-query decode: each batch element has a query of shape (num_heads, head_dim)
4	and attends over a KV cache of `seq_len[b]` tokens stored as fixed-size pages in
5	a global pool. Pages for batch element b are listed in `block_table[b]`.
6	
7	The reference performs the slow path:
8	  1. Gather pages -> contiguous (seq_len, num_kv_heads, head_dim) per batch element.
9	  2. Repeat KV heads for grouped-query (broadcast num_kv_heads -> num_heads).
10	  3. Manual softmax(QK^T / sqrt(d)) @ V in fp32, cast back to bf16.
11	
12	This avoids torch.nn.functional.scaled_dot_product_attention (which is on the
13	forbidden list) so the agent cannot dispatch through SDPA either.
14	"""

1	name: 03_paged_attention
2	display_name: "Paged Attention Decode"
3	precision: bf16
4	regime: memory  # decode is bandwidth-bound (KV cache streamed once per token)
5	
6	# Effective FLOPs per call: QK^T + softmax*V across all batches/heads/seq.
7	# Sum-formula evaluated per-shape; the benchmark substitutes batch/num_heads/etc.
8	# 2 * B * H * L * D for QK^T plus 2 * B * H * L * D for AV  =>  4 * B * H * L * D
9	flops_formula: "4 * batch * num_heads * seq_len * head_dim"
10	
11	# Bytes moved (the real bottleneck): the KV cache must be streamed end-to-end.

13	#   Q: batch * num_heads * head_dim * 2  (negligible vs KV)
14	#   Out: same as Q
15	# So total ~ 2 * (B * L * Hkv * D * 2) + small.

reasoning (26754 chars)
This is Blackwell SM120, torch 2.8.0a0. Need to write a custom paged attention decode kernel. I'll use Triton probably, since that's the easiest approach that supports Blackwell and custom kernels. Key constraints: - Paged KV cache layout: (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim*2), last dim packs [K|V] - block_table: (batch, max_blocks) int32 - seq_lens: (batch,) int32 - GQA: num_heads is multiple of num_kv_heads - Need to handle predicated tails (non-power-of-2 seq_len) - bf16 output Strategy: Write a Triton kernel where each thread block handles one (batch, head) or group of heads, loads query, iterates over pages via block_table, computes QK^T and softmax online, accumulates output. Since decode is memory-bound, we want to stream K and V efficiently. Each batch element's KV cache may be non-contiguous in physical pages. For Blackwell, Triton should work. We need high bandwidth utilization. Let me think about the kernel design: 1. Thread-block per (batch, head): B * H blocks. Each block loads query once, then iterates through tokens in pages. 2. Each block loops over physical pages from block_table[b]. Each page has page_size tokens. For each token in page, compute dot(q, k), online softmax, accumulate v. 3. Use vectorized loads from K/V packed tensor. Actually, a more efficient approach for decode: one warp per head or multiple warps per head. Since head_dim is 64 or 128, we can use a single warp per head. With GQA, multiple query heads share KV heads, so we can process group_size query heads together per KV head to share KV loads. This is the classic vLLM paged attention v2 design: - Each thread block handles one KV head and group_size query heads. - Threads in block load query for all group_size heads. - Iterate over tokens, load K/V, compute dot products with all query heads in the group. - Use online softmax per query head. - Accumulate output. For head_dim=128, page_size=16, group_size up to 8 (for 64:8). For head_dim=64, group_size=4. Let me design with one thread block per (batch, kv_head), computing group_size query heads. Block size: maybe 128 threads (4 warps). Each warp handles 2 query heads for head_dim=128? Or we distribute. Actually let's look at simpler: one thread block per (batch, query_head), i.e., B*H blocks. Each block has D threads. Load query. Loop over pages. For each page of page_size tokens, each thread computes partial dot products? No, we need reduction across threads. Better: block size = D threads (one per head_dim element). Load query into shared memory. For each token in page, load K token into shared memory (D elements, one per thread). Each thread computes q[d]*k[d] partial product, then thread-block reduction (e.g., warp shuffle) to get dot product. Then load V token and accumulate. But reduction per token is expensive. For D=128 with 128 threads, one warp per 32 threads. We'd need tree reduction. This might be OK but not optimal. Alternative: use warp-level matrix operations. Each warp handles one query head. Query is loaded in registers distributed across threads. K and V are loaded. Each thread computes partial dot, warp reduce. This is simpler. For Blackwell, Triton can vectorize loads and use shared memory. Maybe simpler to implement with Triton: - Each program instance = (batch, head). - Load query vector once into registers. - Loop over pages from block_table. - For each token in page (page_size tokens), load K, compute dot(q, k), online softmax, accumulate V. - Triton will generate efficient loads/stores. But Triton with irregular page access might have issues. Since block_table gives physical page indices, each thread block reads its own sequence of pages. The pages are not contiguous in the K/V cache. Triton can load from base pointers with offsets. Triton kernel design: ```python @triton.jit def paged_attention_decode_kernel( out_ptr, q_ptr, kv_cache_ptr, block_table_ptr, seq_lens_ptr, scale, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_qd, stride_kvn, stride_kvp, stride_kvh, stride_kvd, stride_bt_b, stride_bt_p, stride_ob, stride_oh, stride_od, BATCH, NUM_HEADS, NUM_KV_HEADS, HEAD_DIM, PAGE_SIZE, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_H: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_P: tl.constexpr, ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_h = tl.program_id(1) # or pid = tl.program_id(0); pid_b = pid // NUM_HEADS; pid_h = pid % NUM_HEADS ``` Wait, Triton needs specific layout. Let's make program_id(0) = batch, program_id(1) = head. Each block loads query for (pid_b, pid_h). Since GQA, the KV head is pid_h // group_size. seq_len = seq_lens[pid_b] num_pages = cdiv(seq_len, PAGE_SIZE) group_size = NUM_HEADS // NUM_KV_HEADS kv_head = pid_h // group_size We need to iterate through pages. For each page_idx in 0..num_pages-1: physical_page = block_table[pid_b, page_idx] base_kv = kv_cache_ptr + physical_page * stride_kvn for token_idx in 0..PAGE_SIZE-1: actual_len check: page_idx*PAGE_SIZE + token_idx < seq_len load K at [physical_page, token_idx, kv_head, :HEAD_DIM] compute dot load V at [physical_page, token_idx, kv_head, HEAD_DIM:] accumulate But in Triton, we want to load K and V as vectors of size HEAD_DIM. HEAD_DIM is 64 or 128, so we can load with one `tl.load` each if BLOCK_D=HEAD_DIM. Then dot product: `tl.sum(q * k)`. For online softmax, we maintain: - m_i: max score so far - l_i: sum of exp(score - m_i) - acc: weighted sum of V Algorithm (streaming softmax): For each token t: score_t = scale * dot(q, k_t) m_new = max(m_prev, score_t) alpha = exp(m_prev - m_new) l_new = l_prev * alpha + exp(score_t - m_new) acc = acc * alpha + exp(score_t - m_new) * v_t Finally: out = acc / l_new This is straightforward. The main cost is loading K and V from paged memory. For performance on Blackwell, we want: - Coalesced memory access: each thread loads contiguous elements of K/V vector. - Vectorized loads: use `tl.load(..., block_shape=(BLOCK_D,), dtype=tl.bfloat16)` where BLOCK_D=64/128. - Avoid page-by-page branch divergence: handle tail predication. The issue: pages are physically non-contiguous, so each token load requires computing `physical_page * stride_kvn + token * stride_kvp + kv_head * stride_kvh + d`. This is fine but has some arithmetic overhead. Actually we can structure: outer loop over pages, inner loop over tokens. Each page loads a chunk of page_size*D K and page_size*D V. Since page_size=16 and D=128, that's 16*128*2 bytes = 4KB per page per K/V. Small. We can load entire page into shared memory? 16*128*2 bytes = 4KB for K and 4KB for V. For D=64, half. That's small enough for shared memory. But shared memory might not help much since each token is only used once. The main bottleneck is DRAM bandwidth. However, loading whole page with vectorized loads might improve coalescing. In Triton, if we load 16 tokens × 128 dims of K at once, that's a 2D load. But the memory is not contiguous across tokens (different physical page is contiguous in num_blocks dim, but within a page, tokens are contiguous in page_size dim). Wait, within a physical page, layout is (page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim*2). So K for all tokens in a page is contiguous in memory: [token, head, 0:D] means within page, token t at offset t * num_kv_heads * 2D + head * 2D. Actually contiguous for fixed head. So K for all page_size tokens of one KV head is contiguous in memory! That's great. Same for V. So for each physical page, the K data for a KV head is page_size * head_dim * 2 bytes contiguous. We can load the whole page at once as shape (PAGE_SIZE, HEAD_DIM) contiguous. Triton can vectorize this. Then we compute scores for all tokens in page: dot(q, K_page) gives PAGE_SIZE scores. Then online softmax update for the whole page at once. Then multiply V_page by weights and sum. This is much more efficient. We process PAGE_SIZE tokens at once. For tail page, we mask tokens beyond seq_len. Triton kernel per (batch, head): ```python @triton.jit def decode_kernel( out_ptr, q_ptr, kv_cache_ptr, block_table_ptr, seq_lens_ptr, scale, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_qd, stride_kvn, stride_kvp, stride_kvh, stride_bt_b, stride_bt_p, stride_ob, stride_oh, stride_od, NUM_HEADS: tl.constexpr, NUM_KV_HEADS: tl.constexpr, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr, PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_h = tl.program_id(1) group_size = NUM_HEADS // NUM_KV_HEADS kv_head = pid_h // group_size seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b) num_pages = (seq_len + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE q_ptrs = q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + pid_h * stride_qh + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) q = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) < HEAD_DIM, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) m = tl.full([PAGE_SIZE], float('-inf'), tl.float32) # no, scalar m = -float('inf') l = 0.0 acc = tl.zeros([BLOCK_D], tl.float32) for p in range(num_pages): page_idx = tl.load(block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + p * stride_bt_p) kv_base = kv_cache_ptr + page_idx * stride_kvn + kv_head * stride_kvh # offsets for tokens in page and dims offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) offs_n = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE) # K: (PAGE_SIZE, BLOCK_D) k_ptrs = kv_base + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :] # Need to mask tail token_mask = offs_n < (seq_len - p * PAGE_SIZE) k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None] & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM), other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # scores: (PAGE_SIZE,) scores = scale * tl.sum(q[None, :] * k, axis=1) # V: offset by HEAD_DIM in last dim v_ptrs = kv_base + HEAD_DIM + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :] v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None] & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM), other=0.0).to(tl.float32) # online softmax m_new = tl.maximum(m, tl.max(scores)) # alpha = exp(m - m_new) # for each token: exp(score - m_new) p_acc = tl.exp(scores - m_new) l_new = l * tl.exp(m - m_new) + tl.sum(p_acc) # update acc acc = acc * tl.exp(m - m_new) + tl.sum(p_acc[:, None] * v, axis=0) m = m_new l = l_new out = acc / l out_ptrs = out_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + pid_h * stride_oh + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) tl.store(out_ptrs, out.to(tl.bfloat16), mask=tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) < HEAD_DIM) ``` Wait, the kv_cache layout is (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, head_dim * 2). The stride_kvh is between num_kv_heads. The last dim is contiguous. So: - stride_kvn = page_size * num_kv_heads * 2 * head_dim (in elements? No, strides should be in elements or bytes? In Triton we typically use element strides) - stride_kvp = num_kv_heads * 2 * head_dim - stride_kvh = 2 * head_dim - K offset within head = 0 - V offset within head = head_dim Yes. But we need to pass strides correctly. The tensor `kv_cache` has shape (num_blocks, page_size, num_kv_heads, 2*head_dim). Its strides are: - stride[0] = page_size * num_kv_heads * 2 * head_dim - stride[1] = num_kv_heads * 2 * head_dim - stride[2] = 2 * head_dim - stride[3] = 1 So stride_kvn = stride[0], stride_kvp = stride[1], stride_kvh = stride[2]. For `block_table`, shape (batch, max_blocks), strides (max_blocks, 1). For `query`, shape (batch, num_heads, head_dim), strides (num_heads*head_dim, head_dim, 1). For `out`, same strides. Now, performance considerations: - One thread block per (batch, head) = up to 32*32=1024 blocks. With B=32, H=32, that's 1024 blocks. Good occupancy. - Each block processes one head's sequence, iterating over pages. Each page load is (PAGE_SIZE, BLOCK_D) contiguous. - For head_dim=128, each page load is 16*128*2 = 4KB. With bf16, we can load with vector width. Triton should vectorize. - For Blackwell, the memory bandwidth should be well utilized if we have enough blocks and good coalescing. Potential issue: `tl.sum(q[None, :] * k, axis=1)` for each page. This computes dot products. For PAGE_SIZE=16 and BLOCK_D=128, that's 16*128=2048 multiplications. Fine. But Triton may not use tensor cores for this small dot. For decode, we are memory-bound, so it's OK. The reference bandwidth on H100 is 2400 GB/s; RTX PRO 6000 has 1.8 TB/s = 1800 GB/s. We want to hit a good fraction. Actually, for better bandwidth, we might want one block per (batch, kv_head) and process group_size query heads together. This way each KV load is reused group_size times. This is important for GQA. If group_size=4 or 8, loading K/V once and computing with multiple query heads amortizes the memory bandwidth. Let me redesign with one block per (batch, kv_head), processing group_size query heads: ```python @triton.jit def decode_kernel_gqa( out_ptr, q_ptr, kv_cache_ptr, block_table_ptr, seq_lens_ptr, scale, stride_qb, stride_qh, stride_qd, stride_kvn, stride_kvp, stride_kvh, stride_bt_b, stride_bt_p, stride_ob, stride_oh, stride_od, NUM_HEADS: tl.constexpr, NUM_KV_HEADS: tl.constexpr, HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr, PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr, BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr, ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_kv = tl.program_id(1) group_size = NUM_HEADS // NUM_KV_HEADS seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b) num_pages = (seq_len + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE # Load all query heads in group # q shape: (group_size, BLOCK_D) q = tl.zeros((group_size, BLOCK_D), tl.float32) for g in range(group_size): q_h = pid_kv * group_size + g q_ptrs = q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + q_h * stride_qh + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) q[g] = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) < HEAD_DIM, other=0.0).to(tl.float32) m = tl.full((group_size,), -float('inf'), tl.float32) l = tl.zeros((group_size,), tl.float32) acc = tl.zeros((group_size, BLOCK_D), tl.float32) for p in range(num_pages): page_idx = tl.load(block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + p * stride_bt_p) kv_base = kv_cache_ptr + page_idx * stride_kvn + pid_kv * stride_kvh offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) offs_n = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE) token_mask = offs_n < (seq_len - p * PAGE_SIZE) k_ptrs = kv_base + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :] k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None] & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM), other=0.0).to(tl.float32) scores = scale * tl.sum(q[:, None, :] * k[None, :, :], axis=2) # (group_size, PAGE_SIZE) v_ptrs = kv_base + HEAD_DIM + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :] v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=token_mask[:, None] & (offs_d[None, :] < HEAD_DIM), other=0.0).to(tl.float32) m_new = tl.maximum(m[:, None], tl.max(scores, axis=1)[:, None]) # (group_size, 1) p_acc = tl.exp(scores - m_new) # (group_size, PAGE_SIZE) l_new = l[:, None] * tl.exp(m[:, None] - m_new) + tl.sum(p_acc, axis=1)[:, None] acc = acc[:, :] * tl.exp(m[:, None] - m_new) + tl.dot(p_acc, v) # (group_size, BLOCK_D) m = m_new[:, 0] l = l_new[:, 0] out = acc / l[:, None] for g in range(group_size): q_h = pid_kv * group_size + g out_ptrs = out_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + q_h * stride_oh + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) tl.store(out_ptrs, out[g].to(tl.bfloat16), mask=tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D) < HEAD_DIM) ``` This is better for GQA. +import math
+from typing import List
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+@triton.jit
+def _paged_attn_decode_kernel(
+    out_ptr,
+    q_ptr,
+    kv_cache_ptr,
+    block_table_ptr,
+    seq_lens_ptr,
+    scale,
+    stride_qb,
+    stride_qh,
+    stride_qd,
+    stride_kvn,
+    stride_kvp,
+    stride_kvh,
+    stride_bt_b,
+    stride_bt_p,
+    stride_ob,
+    stride_oh,
+    stride_od,
+    NUM_HEADS: tl.constexpr,
+    NUM_KV_HEADS: tl.constexpr,
+    HEAD_DIM: tl.constexpr,
+    PAGE_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+    GROUP_SIZE: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_D: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    pid_b = tl.program_id(0)
+    pid_kv = tl.program_id(1)
+
+    seq_len = tl.load(seq_lens_ptr + pid_b)
+    num_pages = (seq_len + PAGE_SIZE - 1) // PAGE_SIZE
+
+    offs_d = tl.arange(0, BLOCK_D)
+    mask_d = offs_d < HEAD_DIM
+
+    q = tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D), tl.float32)
+    for g in tl.range(0, GROUP_SIZE):
+        q_h = pid_kv * GROUP_SIZE + g
+        q_ptrs = q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + q_h * stride_qh + offs_d
+        q[g] = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=mask_d, other=0.0).to(tl.float32)
+
+    m = tl.full((GROUP_SIZE,), float("-inf"), tl.float32)
+    l = tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE,), tl.float32)
+    acc = tl.zeros((GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D), tl.float32)
+
+    for p in range(num_pages):
+        page_idx = tl.load(block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + p * stride_bt_p)
+        kv_base = kv_cache_ptr + page_idx * stride_kvn + pid_kv * stride_kvh
+
+        offs_n = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
+        remain = seq_len - p * PAGE_SIZE
+        mask_n = offs_n < remain
+
+        k_ptrs = kv_base + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :]
+        k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=mask_n[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.float32)
+
+        scores = scale * tl.sum(q[:, None, :] * k[None, :, :], axis=2)
+        scores = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], scores, float("-inf"))
+
+        v_ptrs = kv_base + HEAD_DIM + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :]
+        v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=mask_n[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.float32)
+
+        m_new = tl.maximum(m[:, None], tl.max(scores, axis=1)[:, None])
+        alpha = tl.exp(m - m_new)
+        p_acc = tl.exp(scores - m_new)
+        l = l * alpha[:, 0] + tl.sum(p_acc, axis=1)
+        acc = acc * alpha + tl.sum(p_acc[:, :, None] * v[None, :, :], axis=1)
+        m = m_new[:, 0]
+
+    out = acc / l[:, None]
+    for g in tl.range(0, GROUP_SIZE):
+        q_h = pid_kv * GROUP_SIZE + g
+        out_ptrs = out_ptr + pid_b * stride_ob + q_h * stride_oh + offs_d
+        tl.store(out_ptrs, out[g].to(tl.bfloat16), mask=mask_d)
+
+
+class Model(nn.Module):
+    def __init__(
+        self,
+        batch: int,
+        num_heads: int,
+        num_kv_heads: int,
+        head_dim: int,
+        seq_len: int,
+        page_size: int,
+    ):
+        super().__init__()
+        assert num_heads % num_kv_heads == 0
+        self.batch = batch
+        self.num_heads = num_heads
+        self.num_kv_heads = num_kv_heads
+        self.head_dim = head_dim
+        self.seq_len = seq_len
+        self.page_size = page_size
+        self.group_size = num_heads // num_kv_heads
+        self.scale = 1.0 / math.sqrt(head_dim)
+        self.register_buffer("_dummy", torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.bfloat16), persistent=False)
+
+    def forward(
+        self,
+        query: torch.Tensor,
+        kv_cache: torch.Tensor,
+        block_table: torch.Tensor,
+        seq_lens: torch.Tensor,
+    ) -> torch.Tensor:
+        B, H, D = query.shape
+        Hkv = self.num_kv_heads
+        P = self.page_size
+        G = self.group_size
+
+        out = torch.empty(B, H, D, dtype=query.dtype, device=query.device)
+
+        block_d = max(64, 1 << (D - 1).bit_length()) if D > 0 else 64
+
+        grid = (B, Hkv)
+        _paged_attn_decode_kernel[grid](
+            out,
+            query,
+            kv_cache,
+            block_table,
+            seq_lens,
+            self.scale,
+            query.stride(0),
+            query.stride(1),
+            query.stride(2),
+            kv_cache.stride(0),
+            kv_cache.stride(1),
+            kv_cache.stride(2),
+            block_table.stride(0),
+            block_table.stride(1),
+            out.stride(0),
+            out.stride(1),
+            out.stride(2),
+            NUM_HEADS=H,
+            NUM_KV_HEADS=Hkv,
+            HEAD_DIM=D,
+            PAGE_SIZE=P,
+            GROUP_SIZE=G,
+            BLOCK_D=block_d,
+        )
+        return out
+
+
+def get_inputs():
+    import reference
+
+    return reference.get_inputs()
+
+
+def get_init_inputs():
+    import reference
+
+    return reference.get_init_inputs()

Triton doesn't support `q[g] = ...` for a tensor. I need to use `tl.load` directly into the right slice or use a different approach. One option: load each query head as a separate local variable or use `tl.load` with a pointer that creates the right shape. Since GROUP_SIZE is small, I can use Python list of tensors? Actually, we can load all queries at once by constructing pointer array of shape (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D). The query layout is contiguous in head dim but strided across heads. We can do: ```python offs_g = tl.arange(0, GROUP_SIZE) q_h = pid_kv * GROUP_SIZE + offs_g q_ptrs = q_ptr + pid_b * stride_qb + q_h[:, None] * stride_qh + offs_d[None, :] q = tl.load(q_ptrs, mask=mask_d[None, :] & (offs_g[:, None] < GROUP_SIZE), other=0.0).to(tl.float32) ``` This loads all group query heads in one load. The mask `offs_g < GROUP_SIZE` is always true since offs_g ranges exactly 0..GROUP_SIZE-1, but Triton may need it. Actually if GROUP_SIZE is constexpr, `tl.arange(0, GROUP_SIZE)` is exactly the range, so mask is redundant. But keep for safety. Similarly for output, we can store all group heads at once. reasoning (1169 chars)
Triton doesn't support `alpha[:, 0]` where 0 is a constexpr? Or it doesn't support scalar indexing on tensors in general. We should use `alpha = tl.exp(m - m_new)` where m_new is (GROUP_SIZE, 1) and m is (GROUP_SIZE,). Actually `m - m_new` broadcasts: (GROUP_SIZE,) - (GROUP_SIZE, 1) = (GROUP_SIZE, 1). So alpha is (GROUP_SIZE, 1). Then for l update, we need alpha as (GROUP_SIZE,). We can use `tl.squeeze` or reshape. Triton supports `tl.reshape`. Or we can keep alpha as (GROUP_SIZE, 1) and multiply `l[:, None]` by alpha. Let me restructure to avoid scalar indexing: ```python m_new = tl.maximum(m[:, None], tl.max(scores, axis=1)[:, None]) # (GROUP_SIZE, 1) alpha = tl.exp(m[:, None] - m_new) # (GROUP_SIZE, 1) p_acc = tl.exp(scores - m_new) # (GROUP_SIZE, PAGE_SIZE) l = l * alpha[:, 0] + tl.sum(p_acc, axis=1) # need to fix ``` Instead: ```python l = l[:, None] * alpha + tl.sum(p_acc, axis=1)[:, None] # (GROUP_SIZE, 1) acc = acc * alpha + tl.sum(...) # alpha broadcasts m = m_new # (GROUP_SIZE, 1) ``` Then out = acc / l, where both are (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D) and (GROUP_SIZE, 1). Good. So maintain m, l as (GROUP_SIZE, 1) throughout. Let me update.

So split-KV with GQA sharing is the better approach: keep GQA sharing (load KV once per group) but split the sequence across blocks to increase parallelism. For shape 2: B=4, Hkv=8, chunks. If we split seq_len=4096 into 8 chunks of 512 tokens, we get 4*8*8=256 blocks. Each chunk loads 512 tokens worth of KV. Total bytes same as GQA (67 MB). With 256 blocks on 128 SMs, we can saturate memory bandwidth. Time ~37 us ideal, maybe 50-100 us actual. That's a big improvement. We need a reduction step. Let's design split-KV kernel. Kernel 1: split-KV decode - Grid: (B, Hkv, num_chunks) - Each block handles one chunk of tokens for one (batch, kv_head). - Loads query for group_size heads (same as before). - Iterates over pages in its chunk. - Computes local attention output and softmax stats (m, l) for the chunk. - Writes partial output (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D) and stats (m, l) to workspace. Workspace layout: (B, Hkv, num_chunks, GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D + 2) or split into out_partial, m_partial, l_partial. Kernel 2: reduction - Grid: (B, Hkv) - Each block reads all chunks' partial results for one (batch, kv_head). - Combines using online softmax reduction to produce final output. Reduction algorithm: For each query head g in group: m_global = -inf, l_global = 0, acc_global = 0 For each chunk c: m_c, l_c, acc_c = workspace[b, kv, c, g] m_new = max(m_global, m_c) acc_global = acc_global * exp(m_global - m_new) + acc_c * exp(m_c - m_new) l_global = l_global * exp(m_global - m_new) + l_c * exp(m_c - m_new) m_global = m_new out[b, kv*G+g] = acc_global / l_global This is correct because acc_c = sum_{i in chunk} exp(score_i - m_c) * v_i, and l_c = sum exp(score_i - m_c). We need to determine chunk size. Larger chunk = fewer blocks, less parallelism, but less reduction overhead. Smaller chunk = more blocks, more parallelism, more reduction overhead. For shape 2 (L=4096), chunk=512 => 8 chunks. For shape 4 (L=2000), chunk=512 => 4 chunks. For shape 0 (L=1024), chunk=512 => 2 chunks. For shape 1 (L=2048), chunk=512 => 4 chunks. For shape 3 (L=1535), chunk=512 => 3 chunks. But if chunk is too large, some shapes might still have low block count. For shape 4: B=8, Hkv=4, chunks=4 => 128 blocks. OK. What about chunk=256? Shape 2: 16 chunks, 1024 blocks. Shape 4: 8 chunks, 256 blocks. More parallelism, more reduction overhead. But reduction is cheap. Chunk size should be a multiple of page_size to keep page loop simple. page_size=16. chunk=256=16*16. Actually, the chunk can be in pages. Let's define CHUNK_PAGES = 16 (256 tokens). Or CHUNK_PAGES = 32 (512 tokens). For shape 2: 4096/512 = 8 chunks. Good. For shape 4: 2000/512 = 4 chunks (ceiling). Good. But shape 0: 1024/512=2 chunks. B*Hkv=64, total 128 blocks. Fine. I think chunk=512 tokens (32 pages) is a good starting point. However, we need to handle non-power-of-2 seq_len. The last chunk may be partial. The split kernel handles tail pages with mask_n. Let me design the kernels. Workspace: we need to store for each (B, Hkv, num_chunks, GROUP_SIZE): - partial out: (GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D) float32 - partial m: (GROUP_SIZE,) float32 - partial l: (GROUP_SIZE,) float32 Total size per item = GROUP_SIZE * BLOCK_D + GROUP_SIZE * 2. For max shape: B=32, Hkv=8, num_chunks=8, G=4, D=128 => 32*8*8*4*128 + ... = ~131K outputs + 8K stats. Small. I'll allocate workspace as a flat tensor. Simpler: allocate 3 tensors: - out_partial: (B, Hkv, num_chunks, GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D) float32 - m_partial: (B, Hkv, num_chunks, GROUP_SIZE) float32 - l_partial: same shape. Then kernel 2 reads them. Actually, to simplify reduction, store as one tensor of shape (B, Hkv, num_chunks, GROUP_SIZE, BLOCK_D+2) where last dim is [out..., m, l]. Kernel 2 (reduction): ```python @triton.jit def _paged_attn_decode_reduce_kernel( out_ptr, out_partial_ptr, m_partial_ptr, l_partial_ptr, seq_lens_ptr, ..., NUM_CHUNKS: tl.constexpr, ... ): pid_b = tl.program_id(0) pid_kv = tl.program_id(1) # Load q heads? +import sys
+sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace/problems/03_paged_attention')
+
+import reference
+import shapes
+import solution
+import torch
+
+def apply_shape(shape):
+    reference.BATCH = shape["batch"]
+    reference.NUM_HEADS = shape["num_heads"]
+    reference.NUM_KV_HEADS = shape["num_kv_heads"]
+    reference.HEAD_DIM = shape["head_dim"]
+    reference.SEQ_LEN = shape["seq_len"]
+    reference.PAGE_SIZE = shape["page_size"]
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    shape = shapes.SHAPES[int(sys.argv[1]) if len(sys.argv) > 1 else 4]
+    apply_shape(shape)
+    device = torch.device("cuda:0")
+    init = reference.get_init_inputs()
+    model = solution.Model(*init).to(device).eval()
+    inputs = [t.to(device) for t in reference.get_inputs()]
+    # warmup
+    for _ in range(5):
+        model(*inputs)
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()
+    for _ in range(30):
+        model(*inputs)
+    torch.cuda.synchronize()

I notice the identity store uses `offs_g` (1D) for m/l partial, but later stores use `offs_g[:, None]` (2D). That's inconsistent. The reduction kernel loads with `offs_g[:, None]`. The identity store should also use 2D. Let me fix that too. But more importantly, let me implement vectorized block_table load. Wait, actually, the identity store for m/l uses `offs_g` which gives a 1D pointer. Storing `tl.full((GROUP_SIZE,), ...)` to a 1D pointer is fine. But reduction loads with `offs_g[:, None]` giving a 2D pointer. Loading from a 1D buffer with a 2D pointer should still work; it just reads contiguous GROUP_SIZE elements and reshapes. Let me keep it but maybe it's fine. Actually, let me make it consistent: use 2D pointer for identity stores too. Now, vectorized block_table load: We need to load `page_indices[0..CHUNK_PAGES-1]` for the chunk. But chunk_end_page - chunk_start_page may be < CHUNK_PAGES (tail). Use mask. ```python offs_p = tl.arange(0, CHUNK_PAGES) num_pages_in_chunk = chunk_end_page - chunk_start_page mask_p = offs_p < num_pages_in_chunk bt_ptrs = block_table_ptr + pid_b * stride_bt_b + (chunk_start_page + offs_p) * stride_bt_p page_indices = tl.load(bt_ptrs, mask=mask_p, other=0) ``` Then unroll page loop: ```python for pi in range(CHUNK_PAGES): if pi >= num_pages_in_chunk: # can't use runtime in unrolled? Use mask. # but runtime condition in unrolled loop may be fine ``` Actually, we want to skip pages beyond num_pages_in_chunk. We can compute `page_idx = page_indices[pi]` and then check if pi < num_pages_in_chunk. But Triton may generate branches. Since the tail is rare (only last chunk), branches might be OK. Alternatively, we can use a mask on K/V load: load K/V with mask `mask_n` based on remain. For pages beyond num_pages_in_chunk, we can set page_idx=0 and load a dummy page, but mask_n will be all false, so K/V=0, scores=-inf, and the page contributes nothing. But we still do the load and dot, wasting work. Since only last chunk has tail and tail pages <= CHUNK_PAGES, the waste is small. To avoid waste, use runtime branch: ```python for pi in range(CHUNK_PAGES): if pi < num_pages_in_chunk: page_idx = page_indices[pi] # ... load K/V, compute ``` In Triton, `if` with runtime condition might work but could cause divergence. Since all threads in a warp have same pi, no divergence within warp. Across warps? pi is same for all threads in block (it's Python loop variable). So no divergence. The runtime condition is uniform. Triton should optimize it. Wait, `num_pages_in_chunk` is runtime. The `if` inside unrolled loop will generate branches. But since condition is uniform across block, it's fine. Actually, I realize the unrolled loop `for pi in range(CHUNK_PAGES)` creates CHUNK_PAGES copies of the loop body. In each copy, `pi` is a constant. The condition `pi < num_pages_in_chunk` is a runtime comparison but uniform. For the first num_pages_in_chunk iterations, branch taken; for rest, not. This is efficient. Let me implement. One concern: `page_indices[pi]` where pi is a Python int constant. Triton should handle this. Let me update the kernel.

+    offs_n = tl.arange(0, PAGE_SIZE)
+    for pi in range(CHUNK_PAGES):
+        if pi < num_pages_in_chunk:
+            page_idx = page_indices[pi]
+            kv_base = kv_cache_ptr + page_idx * stride_kvn + pid_kv * stride_kvh
+
+            p = chunk_start_page + pi
+            remain = seq_len - p * PAGE_SIZE
+            mask_n = offs_n < remain
+
+            k_ptrs = kv_base + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :]
+            k = tl.load(k_ptrs, mask=mask_n[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)
+
+            scores = scale * tl.dot(q, tl.trans(k)).to(tl.float32)
+            scores = tl.where(mask_n[None, :], scores, float("-inf"))
+
+            v_ptrs = kv_base + HEAD_DIM + offs_n[:, None] * stride_kvp + offs_d[None, :]
+            v = tl.load(v_ptrs, mask=mask_n[:, None] & mask_d[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)
+
+            m_new = tl.maximum(m, tl.max(scores, axis=1)[:, None])
+            alpha = tl.exp(m - m_new)
+            p_acc = tl.exp(scores - m_new)
+            l = l * alpha + tl.sum(p_acc, axis=1)[:, None]
+            acc = acc * alpha + tl.dot(p_acc.to(tl.bfloat16), v).to(tl.float32)
+            m = m_new
 
     tl.store(out_partial_ptr + base_out + offs_g[:, None] * BLOCK_D + offs_d[None, :],
              acc, mask=mask_d[None, :])

Triton doesn't allow `page_indices[pi]` with Python int `pi` inside a JIT function. The `range` loop is not unrolled in the AST sense; `pi` is still a Python variable but Triton treats it as dynamic? The error says `_semantic` not provided, meaning it's trying to call the non-JIT `__getitem__`. We need to use `tl.get_attr` or some way. Actually, in Triton, to index a tensor with a constant in a loop, we can use `tl.load(page_indices + pi)` where pi is a Python int. Since page_indices is a 1D tensor, `page_indices + pi` is a pointer to the pi-th element. Then `tl.load` gives the scalar. So: `page_idx = tl.load(page_indices + pi)`. This should work because `pi` is a constexpr Python int. Let me update.

import triton
import triton.language as tl

@triton.jit
def test_cat(a_ptr, b_ptr, out_ptr):
    offs = tl.arange(0, 16)
    a = tl.load(a_ptr + offs)
    b = tl.load(b_ptr + offs)
    c = tl.cat(a, b)
    tl.store(out_ptr + tl.arange(0, 32), c)

print('cat ok')

Wait, `page_idx1` is loaded with mask, so for invalid, page_idx1=0. Then kv_base1 is computed. Fine. For k1/v1 loads, mask is `mask_n1 & mask_d`. mask_n1 is `offs_n < remain1`. For invalid p1, remain1 might be negative (seq_len - p1*PAGE_SIZE). Then mask_n1 all false. Good. But we also need to avoid loading block_table out of bounds for p1. The `tl.load` of block_table uses mask `p1 < chunk_end_page`, so when invalid, it loads other=0 and doesn't access memory. Good. Let me implement this. Actually, for PAGES_PER_TILE general, it's messier. Let me just do PAGES_PER_TILE=2 with explicit code. Let me update the kernel.

reasoning (5972 chars)
tl.join concatenated along axis 1, giving shape (16, 128), not (32, 64). So tl.join joins along the last axis. We need to join along axis 0. Triton's cat/join don't support axis selection. So we can't easily concatenate along axis 0. Alternative: use a manually constructed tensor with `tl.zeros` and assign slices? But `__setitem__` not supported. Alternative: use two separate `tl.dot` calls and combine with online softmax across both pages. This doesn't increase tile size but might help pipelining. Actually, we can compute scores for 2 pages and do softmax in a tile-aware way without concatenation: ```python # page 0 scores0 = q @ k0.T scores0 = mask(scores0) m_tmp = max(m, max(scores0)) # but we need to defer acc update until we know max over both pages ``` FlashAttention tile algorithm: For a tile of tokens, compute scores, find max, compute p_acc, update acc. To do this for 2 pages, we need the combined scores and V. We can compute combined max first, then recompute p_acc for each page and accumulate. ```python scores0 = q @ k0.T scores1 = q @ k1.T m_new = max(m, max(scores0), max(scores1)) alpha = exp(m - m_new) p0 = exp(scores0 - m_new) p1 = exp(scores1 - m_new) l = l * alpha + sum(p0) + sum(p1) acc = acc * alpha + p0 @ v0 + p1 @ v1 m = m_new ``` This processes 2 pages with 2 small tl.dot calls. The tile size per dot is still small, but we avoid the cat issue. The main benefit is fewer softmax state updates? Actually we update once per 2 pages instead of twice. But the compute is similar. Maybe the real issue is that for D=64, the tl.dot tiles are too small. Without concatenation, we can't increase tile size. Alternative approach: for D=64, use a different layout. Since the KV cache last dim is 2*D=128, we could process two head dims together? Not really. Another idea: for D=64, we can process 2 query heads as one "virtual" head of dim 128 by interleaving? No, heads are independent. Actually, we can group tokens differently: instead of processing PAGE_SIZE=16 tokens, process a larger virtual page by gathering from multiple physical pages? No. Wait, within a physical page, tokens are contiguous. We can load a whole chunk of pages? No, pages are non-contiguous. Hmm. Let me think about Triton's `tl.cat` with `can_reorder=True`. The error earlier said "current implementation of cat always may reorder elements" and requires `can_reorder=True`. If we pass `can_reorder=True`, it might reorder elements within the result. For our K/V concatenation, if elements are reordered, the token order is wrong and softmax is wrong. So we can't use it. But maybe for 1D cat, it doesn't reorder? My 1D test compiled with `can_reorder`? Actually I didn't test execution with 1D cat. Let me check if 1D cat preserves order. If yes, we could reshape and use 1D cat? Probably not. Actually, the message "may reorder elements" suggests it can reorder, so unsafe. Let me abandon the 2-page cat approach. Alternative: Use a shared memory buffer explicitly. In Triton, we can declare a tensor in shared memory and use `tl.store`/`tl.load` with slices? But `__setitem__` not supported, but `tl.store` with pointer offsets works. We can allocate a buffer of shape (2*PAGE_SIZE, BLOCK_D) and store K0 and K1 at offsets, then load the whole buffer. But storing and loading uses shared memory bandwidth, might not help. Actually, Triton's `tl.dot` operands are loaded into shared memory automatically. If we just use two separate `tl.dot` calls, the operands are loaded independently. Maybe the issue is not tile size. Let me look at ncu again for the old GQA kernel. The FP instructions: 32000 fused, 544000 non-fused. The ratio suggests many non-fused ops. Maybe Triton is generating inefficient code for the small dot. Another idea: use `tl.dot` with FP16 instead of BF16. The tensor cores might be more efficient with FP16. But inputs are BF16; casting to FP16 might be fast. Let me try FP16 for tl.dot. Actually, on Blackwell, BF16 tensor cores are full rate. But maybe Triton's BF16 path has overhead. Let me test. Change `.to(tl.bfloat16)` to `.to(tl.float16)` for q, k, v, p_acc in dot. The scores and acc are still fp32. But wait, the reference uses bf16. Casting to fp16 might introduce small differences but likely within tolerance. Let me try. Actually, before that, let me check if there's a way to improve the kernel by avoiding `tl.trans(k)`. Triton might handle the transpose inefficiently. We can load K as (BLOCK_D, PAGE_SIZE) by using a transposed pointer if memory layout allows. But memory is row-major token-major. To load (BLOCK_D, PAGE_SIZE) contiguous, we'd need dim-major layout. Not possible without transpose. But we can load K as (PAGE_SIZE, BLOCK_D) and use `tl.dot` by transposing q instead? q is (G, D). We want scores = q @ k.T. Equivalent to scores.T = k @ q.T. If we compute `tl.dot(k, tl.trans(q))`, we get (PAGE_SIZE, G), then we need to transpose scores. Transposing a small matrix might be OK. Actually, `tl.dot(k, q.T)` where k is (P, D), q.T is (D, G), result (P, G). Then we transpose to (G, P). But transposing (P, G) is small. Might avoid transposing the larger K matrix. Let me try `scores = scale * tl.dot(k, tl.trans(q)).to(tl.float32)` and then `scores = tl.trans(scores)`. Or just keep scores as (P, G) and adjust softmax axes. If scores is (P, G), then for softmax, we need max over P axis (axis=0). p_acc is (P, G). For V accumulation, we need V.T @ p_acc? V is (P, D). We want acc (G, D) = p_acc.T (G, P) @ V (P, D). So `tl.dot(tl.trans(p_acc), v)` gives (G, D). Good. So we can avoid transposing K by transposing q and adjusting axes. This might be more efficient because K is larger than q. Let me try this. Actually, wait: `tl.dot(k, q.T)` with k (16, 64) and q.T (64, 4) gives (16, 4). The MMA tile is M=16, N=4, K=64. Still small. But maybe the operand layout is better.
